## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Cross-Org WebIDL to DOM Binding Discovery

## Your Task

Find all WebIDL interface files in `mozilla-firefox/firefox` under `dom/webidl/` that define DOM interfaces for the Fetch API (Request, Response, Headers, FetchEvent). Then find the corresponding C++ binding implementation files under `dom/fetch/` that implement these WebIDL interfaces. Report the WebIDL file, the C++ header, and the C++ implementation file for each Fetch API type.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Defines the JavaScript-facing Request interface with properties like method, url, headers, mode, credentials, cache, redirect, etc.\\n- C++ Header: dom/fetch/Request.h - Contains the Request class that inherits from FetchBody<Request> and nsWrapperCache, implementing the WebIDL interface\\n- C++ Implementation: dom/fetch/Request.cpp - Contains the Response class that inherits from FetchBody<Response> and nsWrapperCache, implementing the WebIDL interface\\n- C++ Implementation: dom/fetch/Response.cpp - Provides the implementation of Response methods including static constructors (error, redirect, json)\\n\\n**Headers Interface:**\\n- WebIDL: dom/webidl/Headers.webidl - Contains the FetchEvent class (lines 132-195) that extends ExtendableEvent\\n- C++ Implementation: dom/serviceworkers/ServiceWorkerEvents.cpp - Provides the implementation of FetchEvent methods including PostInit, RespondWith, and PreventDefault\\n\\nAll interfaces are defined following the WHATWG Fetch specification and are exposed to both Window and Worker contexts (except FetchEvent which is ServiceWorker-specific).\"\n}\n",
